<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Confirms profit outlook for 2014; reduces organic revenue growth target to approximately 3% to reflect slower global category growth
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">DEERFIELD, Ill. &#150; May&nbsp;7, 2014 &#150; Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) today reported solid
first quarter 2014 results. Separately, the company announced that it intends to combine its coffee portfolio with D.E Master Blenders 1753 B.V.&#146;s coffee business to create the world&#146;s leading pure-play coffee company. Upon closing,
Mondel&#275;z International will receive after-tax cash proceeds of approximately $5 billion and a 49 percent interest in the new company. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company also announced plans to reduce operating costs to best-in-class levels through a restructuring program that is expected to deliver cost savings of at least $1.5 billion by 2018, providing additional
opportunity for margin expansion beyond its revised 2016 target of 15 to 16 percent. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">1 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;The strategic and cost-reduction actions we announced today underscore our determination to
become a leaner, more focused and more nimble global snacking powerhouse,&#148; said Irene Rosenfeld, Chairman and CEO. &#147;As our first quarter results show, we&#146;re making meaningful progress toward our margin goals, while continuing to
deliver solid growth and market shares. These strategic and cost-reduction actions will strengthen our core snacking business, simplify our operations and enhance our ability to deliver world-class margins. At the same time, our shareholders will
continue to share in the future growth of the coffee category through our ownership interest in an advantaged, more focused coffee company.&#148; </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>Creating the World&#146;s Leading Pure-Play Coffee Company </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Also today, Mondel&#275;z International announced its intention to combine its wholly owned coffee business with D.E Master Blenders 1753 B.V. to create the world&#146;s leading pure-play coffee company. The new
company, to be called Jacobs Douwe Egberts, will hold leading positions in more than two dozen countries and have a strong emerging markets presence in the $81 billion global coffee category. With greater focus and increased scale, the new company
will be able to operate more efficiently and invest more effectively in innovation, manufacturing and market development to capitalize on the significant growth opportunities in coffee. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Jacobs Douwe Egberts is expected to have total revenue of more than $7 billion (<FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#128;</FONT><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"></FONT>5 billion) and an EBITDA margin in the high-teens. In 2013, Mondel&#275;z International&#146;s coffee business generated approximately $3.9 billion
(<FONT STYLE="font-family:Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#128;</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"></FONT>2.9 billion) in revenue with an EBITDA margin in the high-teens. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Upon completion of the proposed transactions, Mondel&#275;z International will receive after-tax cash of approximately $5 billion and a 49 percent
interest in Jacobs Douwe Egberts, enabling its shareholders to share in the synergies and future growth of the new company. Mondel&#275;z International expects the transactions to be completed in the course of 2015, subject to limited closing
conditions, including regulatory approvals. The company expects the transactions to be accretive to earnings in the first full year following close. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company expects to use the majority of its cash proceeds to expand its share repurchase program, subject to approval by the Board of Directors, with the balance used for debt reduction and general corporate
purposes. The company remains committed to maintaining an investment-grade credit rating and access to Tier 2 commercial paper. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>Targeting
Best-in-Class Cost Levels </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In conjunction with the proposed coffee transaction, Mondelez International also announced its plan to
create a leaner, simpler and more focused organization by reducing operating costs to best-in-class levels through zero-based budgeting and by accelerating its supply chain reinvention initiative. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">To facilitate these efforts, the Board of Directors approved a $3.5 billion restructuring program through 2018 (the &#147;2014-2018 Restructuring
Program&#148;), comprised of approximately $2.5 billion in cash costs and $1 billion in non-cash costs. The restructuring program is intended primarily to cover severance as well as asset disposals and other manufacturing-related one-time costs. The
company </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">2 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">
expects to incur the majority of the program&#146;s charges in 2015 and 2016. The $2.2 billion of capital expenditures to support the restructuring program are already included within the
company&#146;s previous guidance of approximately 5 percent of net revenues for the next few years. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company expects the 2014-2018
Restructuring Program to generate annualized savings of at least $1.5 billion by 2018. Lower overheads and accelerated supply chain cost reductions are each expected to generate roughly half of the total incremental savings. Overhead reductions will
be driven by both lower headcount and non-headcount costs. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;Today&#146;s coffee announcement creates an opportunity to further
reduce our supply chain and overhead costs and fast-track the implementation of best-in-class cost management practices on a global basis,&#148; said Dave Brearton, Executive Vice President and CFO. &#147;The savings generated by this new
restructuring program will enable us to accelerate our margin improvement program. Specifically, we&#146;re raising the bottom end of our 2016 Adjusted Operating Income margin target, resulting in a revised range of 15 to 16 percent, up from our
previous target of 14 to 16 percent. After 2016, we expect the cost savings will provide additional fuel to fund growth and drive further margin expansion.&#148; </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>First Quarter Results </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In the first quarter, the company delivered Organic Net Revenue growth
in line with expectations, strong Adjusted Operating Income margin improvement and double-digit growth in both Adjusted Operating Income and Adjusted EPS on a constant currency basis. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%;padding-bottom:0px; "><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">On a reported basis, net revenues were $8.6 billion, down 1.2 percent, and operating income was $843 million, up 1.1 percent.
Diluted EPS was $0.09, including a negative 18 cents from the loss on debt extinguishment</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">3</SUP></FONT><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"> and a negative 9 cents from the remeasurement of net monetary assets in Venezuela</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">4</SUP></FONT><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">3 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I><U>Organic Net Revenue Commentary </U></I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Organic Net Revenue increased 2.8 percent, including a negative 0.6 percentage point impact from lower coffee revenues, reflecting the pass-through of lower green coffee costs. Overall, pricing was up 2.5
percentage points, as the company increased prices across most non-coffee categories in every region. Volume/mix was up slightly despite these higher prices. The 0.4 percentage point headwind from Easter shifting to the second quarter was lower than
expected. Market share performance was strong, with over 60 percent of revenues gaining or holding share. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%;padding-bottom:0px; "><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Organic
Net Revenue from emerging markets</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">5</SUP></FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"> was up 6.7 percent and developed
markets</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">6</SUP></FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"> increased 0.2 percent. Overall, Power Brands grew 4.8 percent.
<I>Tuc, Club Social, belVita</I> and <I>Chips Ahoy!</I> biscuits, <I>Cadbury Dairy Milk</I> and <I>Milka</I> chocolate and <I>Tang </I>powdered beverages each posted at least high single-digit increases. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">On a regional basis, highlights include: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Latin America increased 14.7 percent, largely driven by pricing gains, especially in the inflationary economies of Venezuela and Argentina. Brazil grew high
single digits, as strong double-digit growth in powdered beverages and biscuits was partially offset by the impact from the later timing of Easter on chocolate. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Asia Pacific was down 2.7 percent. Lower volume/mix was mostly attributable to China where difficult prior year comparisons in biscuits more than offset a strong
performance in gum. India delivered another strong quarter with mid-teens growth driven by chocolate and powdered beverages. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">EEMEA was up 7.9 percent, reflecting strong volume/mix gains and modest pricing. Revenue growth in the region was broad-based, with a high single-digit gain in
Russia, and strong double-digit growth in the GCC</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">7 </SUP></FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">countries, Turkey and
Egypt, more than offsetting a double-digit decline in Ukraine due to political and economic instability. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Europe was down 1.0 percent. Pricing in the region was lower, reflecting the pass-through of lower green coffee costs. Lower coffee revenues tempered growth by
1.5 percentage points. Volume/mix increased nearly 1 percentage point despite the impacts of the Easter shift and short-term customer disputes associated with price increases in non-coffee categories. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">North America increased 2.5 percent, driven by continued strong share performance and mid-single digit growth in biscuits. Growth in the category was balanced
between volume/mix and pricing. The rate of decline in gum continued to moderate as U.S. market share was up for the third consecutive quarter. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I><U>Adjusted Operating Income and EPS commentary </U></I></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%;padding-bottom:0px; "><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Adjusted Gross Profit</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP
STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">1</SUP></FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"> increased 2.3 percent on a constant currency basis. Adjusted Gross Margin was essentially flat to prior year, as higher prices
and a strong contribution from supply chain productivity more than offset input cost inflation. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Adjusted Operating Income grew 15.8
percent on a constant currency basis, driven by lower SG&amp;A expense and higher gross profit. Overhead costs declined as a result of the company&#146;s continued cost management efforts. Advertising and consumer support expense was also lower as
the company cycled significantly higher investments in the prior year and drove efficiencies by consolidating media providers, reducing non-working media costs and shifting spending to lower-cost, digital media outlets. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%;padding-bottom:0px; "><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Adjusted EPS grew 17.1 percent on a constant currency basis, driven entirely by operating gains. Below operating income, the
benefits from the share buyback program and lower interest expense were more than offset by an effective tax rate of 20.7 percent compared to 4.0 percent in the prior year</FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="1"><SUP
STYLE="vertical-align:baseline; position:relative; bottom:.8ex">1</SUP></FONT><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>Share Repurchases
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">During the first quarter, the company repurchased $0.5 billion of its common stock at an average price of $34.20 per share.

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;With a solid first quarter, we remain on track to deliver strong gains in Adjusted Operating Income and
Adjusted EPS,&#148; said Brearton. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;On the top line, however, growth in our global categories has slowed to around 3 percent over
the last two quarters, due largely to the weakness in emerging markets and lower coffee prices. We expect these trends will continue in Q2, likely resulting in top-line growth similar to what we saw in Q1. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;While we expect the pass-through of higher green coffee costs will benefit top-line growth as the year unfolds, we anticipate that the
challenging environment in emerging markets will continue and that we may realize some disruptions as we implement our strategic initiatives. As a result, we expect revenue growth to improve modestly in the second half. For the full year, we expect
our Organic Net Revenue growth to be in line with global category growth of approximately 3 percent.&#148; </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>Conference Call </B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Mondel&#275;z International will host a conference call for investors with accompanying slides to review its results at 10 a.m. ET today. Access to
a live audio webcast with accompanying slides and a replay of the event will be available at <U>www.mondelezinternational.com/Investor</U>. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>About
Mondel&#275;z International </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:8%"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. (NASDAQ: MDLZ) is a global snacking powerhouse, with 2013 revenue of
$35 billion. Creating delicious moments of joy in 165 countries, Mondel&#275;z International is a world leader in biscuits, chocolate, gum, candy, coffee and powdered beverages, with billion-dollar brands such as <I>Oreo</I>, <I>LU</I> and
<I>Nabisco</I> biscuits; <I>Cadbury, Cadbury Dairy Milk </I>and <I>Milka</I> chocolate; <I>Trident</I> gum; <I>Jacobs</I> coffee and <I>Tang</I> powdered beverages. Mondel&#275;z International is a proud member of the Standard and Poor&#146;s 500,
NASDAQ 100 and Dow Jones Sustainability Index. Visit <U>www.mondelezinternational.com</U> and <U>www.facebook.com/mondelezinternational</U>. </FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="4"><B>Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="4"><B>Reconciliation of GAAP and Non-GAAP Financial Measures </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="4"><B>(Unaudited) </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company reports its financial results in accordance with accounting principles generally
accepted in the United States (&#147;GAAP&#148; or referred to herein as &#147;Reported&#148;). However, management believes that certain non-GAAP financial measures should be considered when assessing the company&#146;s ongoing performance to
provide more complete information on the factors and trends affecting the company&#146;s business. Management also uses these non-GAAP financial measures in making financial, operating and planning decisions and in evaluating the company&#146;s
performance. Non-GAAP financial measures should be viewed in addition to, and not as an alternative for, the company&#146;s Reported results prepared in accordance with GAAP. In addition, the non-GAAP measures the company uses may differ from
non-GAAP measures used by other companies. Because GAAP financial measures on a forward-looking basis are neither accessible nor deemed to be significantly different from the non-GAAP financial measures, and reconciling information is not available
without unreasonable effort, the company has not provided that information with regard to the non-GAAP financial measures in the company&#146;s Outlook. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>DEFINITIONS OF THE COMPANY&#146;S NON-GAAP FINANCIAL MEASURES </B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company&#146;s non-GAAP financial measures and corresponding metrics reflect how the company evaluates its operating results currently and provide improved
comparability of operating results. As new events or circumstances arise, these definitions could change over time: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;Organic Net Revenues&#148; is defined as net revenues excluding the impacts of acquisitions, divestitures (including businesses under sales agreements and
exits of major product lines under a sale or licensing agreement), Integration Program costs, accounting calendar changes and foreign currency rate fluctuations. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">&#147;Adjusted Gross Profit&#148; is defined as gross profit excluding the impacts of pension costs related to obligations transferred in the Spin-Off, the
2012-2014 Restructuring Program, the Integration Program and other acquisition integration costs and the operating results of divestitures (including businesses under sales agreements and exits of major product lines under a sale or licensing
agreement). We also evaluate growth in the company&#146;s Adjusted Gross Profit on a constant currency basis. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>SEGMENT OPERATING INCOME </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company uses segment operating
income to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. The company believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze segment performance and trends. Segment operating income excludes unrealized gains and losses on
hedging activities (which are a component of cost of sales), general corporate expenses (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses), amortization of intangibles, gains and losses on divestitures and acquisitions and
acquisition-related costs (which are a component of selling, general and administrative expenses) in all periods presented. The company excludes these items from segment operating income in order to provide better transparency of our segment
operating results. Furthermore, the company centrally manages interest and other expense, net. Accordingly, the company does not present these items by segment because they are excluded from the segment profitability measure that management reviews.
</FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">13 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B>ITEMS IMPACTING COMPARABILITY OF OPERATING RESULTS </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The following information is provided to give qualitative and quantitative information related to items impacting comparability of operating results. The company determines which items to consider as &#147;items
impacting comparability&#148; based on how management views the company&#146;s business; makes financial, operating and planning decisions; and evaluates the company&#146;s ongoing performance. In addition, the company provides the impact that
changes in currency exchange rates had on the company&#146;s financial results (referred to as &#147;constant currency&#148;). </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Divestitures
</I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company excludes the operating results of businesses divested, including businesses under sales agreements and exits of major product lines
under a sale or licensing agreement. The company did not divest any businesses during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014. During the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013, we entered into sales agreements to divest two businesses within the
company&#146;s EEMEA segment. These sales agreements related to a salty snacks business in Turkey and a confectionery business in South Africa. In order to evaluate the company&#146;s results from ongoing operations, these transactions are included
in determining the impact from divestitures in evaluating the company&#146;s non-GAAP financial measures. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Acquisition </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">On February&nbsp;22, 2013, the company acquired the remaining interest in a biscuit operation in Morocco, which is now a wholly-owned subsidiary within the
company&#146;s EEMEA segment. The company paid net cash consideration of $119 million, consisting of a $155 million purchase price net of cash acquired of $36 million. Prior to the acquisition, the company&#146;s interest in the operation was
accounted for under the equity method. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Integration Program and other acquisition integration costs </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I>Integration Program costs </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Integration Program costs are
defined as the costs associated with combining the Mondel&#275;z International and Cadbury businesses, and are separate from those costs associated with the acquisition. At the end of 2013, the company completed incurring charges related to the
Integration Program, and during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014, the company recorded a reversal of $2 million related to accruals no longer required. During the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013, the company recorded charges of $21
million in selling, general and administrative expenses within our Europe, Asia Pacific, Latin America and EEMEA segments. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">14 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I>Other acquisition integration costs </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In connection with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Morocco in February 2013, the company recorded integration charges of $1 million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014. The company recorded
these charges in selling, general and administrative expenses within the company&#146;s EEMEA segment. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Spin-Off Costs </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Spin-Off Costs represent transaction, transition and financing and related costs associated with preparing the businesses (Mondel&#275;z International and Kraft
Foods Group) for independent operations and historically consisted primarily of financial advisory fees, legal fees, accounting fees, tax services and information systems infrastructure duplication, and financing and related costs to redistribute
debt and secure investment grade ratings for both the Kraft Foods Group business and the Mondel&#275;z International business. The company recorded Spin-Off Costs of $3 million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014 as compared to $9
million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>2012-2014 Restructuring Program </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In 2012, the company&#146;s Board of Directors approved $1.5 billion of restructuring and related implementation costs (&#147;2012-2014 Restructuring Program&#148;)
reflecting primarily severance, asset disposals and other manufacturing-related one-time costs. The primary objective of the restructuring and implementation activities was to ensure that both Mondel&#275;z International and Kraft Foods Group were
each set up to operate efficiently and execute on the company&#146;s respective business strategies upon separation and in the future. Of the $1.5 billion of anticipated 2012-2014 Restructuring Program costs, the company retained approximately $925
million and Kraft Foods Group retained the balance of the program. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I>Restructuring costs </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company recorded within asset impairment and exit costs charges of $42 million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014 as compared to $40 million in the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013. These
charges were related to asset write-downs (including accelerated depreciation and asset impairments), severance and other related costs. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><I>Implementation costs </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Implementation costs are directly
attributable to restructuring activities; however, they do not qualify for accounting treatment as exit or disposal activities. The company recorded implementation costs of $24 million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2014 as compared to
$4 million during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013. Implementation costs primarily include costs to reorganize the company&#146;s operations and facilities, the discontinuance of certain product lines and the incremental expenses related
to the closure of facilities, replicating the company&#146;s information systems infrastructure and reorganizing costs related to the company&#146;s sales function. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">15 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Remeasurement of Venezuelan Net Monetary Assets </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">As a result of recent Venezuelan currency exchange developments and the expected impact on the company&#146;s Venezuelan operations, the company remeasured its Venezuelan bolivar-denominated net monetary assets as
of March&nbsp;31, 2014 from the official exchange rate of 6.30 to the SICAD I exchange rate of 10.70 bolivars to the U.S. dollar. The company recognized a $142 million currency remeasurement loss within selling, general&nbsp;&amp; administrative
expenses. In addition, due to the company&#146;s underlying legal structure, higher taxes of $8 million were recognized due to interest deductibility limitations resulting from Venezuela&#146;s lower earnings. As of March&nbsp;31, 2014, the
company&#146;s remaining bolivar-denominated net monetary assets were approximately $200 million. The company&#146;s Venezuela net revenues, translated at the 6.30 official rate prior to the remeasurement, were approximately $240 million or 2.8% of
consolidated net revenues in the first quarter of 2014. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013, we also recorded a $54 million currency
remeasurement charge related to the devaluation of the company&#146;s net monetary assets in Venezuela at that time. In addition, due to the company&#146;s underlying legal structure, higher taxes of $5 million were recorded due primarily to
interest deductibility limitations resulting from Venezuela&#146;s lower earnings. As described in our Form 8-K dated April&nbsp;22, 2014, this 2013 remeasurement charge was previously included in our non-GAAP financial measures of Adjusted
Operating Income and Adjusted Earnings Per Share. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">The company continues to monitor developments in the currency and actively manage its investment and
exposures in Venezuela. If any of the rates, or application of the rates to the company&#146;s business, were to change, the company would recognize additional currency losses or gains, which could be significant. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Loss on debt extinguishment and related costs </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">On
February&nbsp;6, 2014, the company completed a $1.6 billion cash tender offer for some of its outstanding high coupon long term debt. The company recorded a pre-tax loss on debt extinguishment and related expenses of $494 million for the amount paid
in excess of the carrying value of the debt and from recognizing unamortized financing discounts and deferred financing costs. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Gain on
acquisition </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In connection, with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Morocco in February 2013, the company recorded a pre-tax gain of $22
million related to the remeasurement of the company&#146;s previously-held equity interest in the operation to fair value in accordance with GAAP. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">16 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Acquisition-related costs </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">In connection, with the acquisition of a biscuit operation in Morocco in February 2013, the company recorded $7 million in acquisition costs during the three months ended March&nbsp;31, 2013, which were included
within selling, general and administrative expenses and interest and other expense. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2"><B><I>Constant currency </I></B></FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Management evaluates the operating performance of the company and its international subsidiaries on a constant currency basis. The company determines its constant
currency operating results by dividing or multiplying, as appropriate, the current period local currency operating results by the currency exchange rates used to translate the company&#146;s financial statements in the comparable prior year period
to determine what the current period U.S. dollar operating results would have been if the currency exchange rate had not changed from the comparable prior year period. </FONT></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">17 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Mondel&#275;z International, Inc. and Subsidiaries </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Reconciliation of GAAP to Non-GAAP Measures
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">Net Revenues </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT STYLE="font-family:ARIAL" SIZE="2">(in millions
